## Current State of the Proof

The Grail conjecture: η(C_p^r) = (9·2^{r-3} - 1)(p-1) + 1 for all r ≥ 3, all odd primes p.

Equivalently: α(r) + 1 = 9·2^{r-3} non-proportional vectors with multiplicity p-1 must contain a zero-sum of weight ≤ p.

### What's proved:

For weight ≡ 1 (mod p), the only way to get weight 1 is impossible with nonzero vectors. The next possibility is weight s where s nonzero coordinates each equal 1, giving s ≡ 1 (mod p). Since s ≤ r+2 ≤ p, the only values satisfying s ≡ 1 (mod p) are s = 1 (impossible) or s = p+1 (too large).

## The Fundamental Tension

The core issue is:
- We can find zero-sums in RANK r-1 (by induction), but they have UNCONSTRAINED first coordinate.
- Adjusting the first coordinate costs weight.
- Weight budget is tight (≤ p total).

**The missing ingredient**: a way to produce zero-sums in F_p^{r-1} whose lifts to F_p^r are ALREADY close to zero-sums, i.e., whose residues are zero or small.

**What if we project along a different subspace?** Instead of quotienting by a 1-dimensional subspace, what about a 2-dimensional one?

Projecting down to F_p^{r-2} by quotienting out a 2-dim subspace V₂ means our n vectors project to at most n images in the lower space, each appearing with multiplicity p-1. Since n is large enough relative to the dimension (α(r)/α(r-2) ≈ 4), we can find a zero-sum of length ≤ p in F_p^{r-2}. The residue of this lift lives in V₂ ≅ F_p², and we'd need to correct it using vectors from V₂ itself. The key observation is that vectors mapping to zero in F_p^{r-2} are exactly those in V₂, so if enough of our original vectors land in V₂, we might be able to balance the residue without exceeding our weight budget.

But this introduces even more moving parts—we'd need to carefully manage which vectors fall in V₂ and whether we have enough flexibility to adjust. This feels like it's adding complexity rather than resolving it.

Let me step back and try something completely different: the inverse sumset perspective from additive combinatorics.

If S is zero-sum free with size α(r)+1 in this setting, what structural constraints follow? Thinking of S as a subset of projective space, the constraint is that no dependency has weight ≤ p. The Davenport constant for C_p^r is r(p-1)+1, and with n = α(r) = 9·2^{r-3}-1, which is much larger than r, there are many dependencies present—the key is that all of them must have weight exceeding p.

For generic vectors, the minimum dependency weight grows with support size until it reaches r, since r independent vectors plus one dependent vector gives a dependency of support size at most r+1. Rather than continue exploring every angle, I should focus on what's actually provable here.

The highest-value contributions right now are a clean formulation of the Partition Dichotomy and an unconditional result that moves beyond the conditional framework. Let me pursue the second: can I establish something unconditional? I'm considering a Multiplicity Amplification Theorem—if we had vectors with higher multiplicity m instead of p-1, would η decrease? This would define η_m(C_p^r) as the smallest n such that any n nonzero non-proportional vectors in F_p^r, each with multiplicity m, must contain a weight-≤p zero-sum.

Now I'm examining what happens when m ≥ p.
